==========================================================================================
  COLUMN DEFINITIONS
==========================================================================================

  REC        : Record index (0-based), order as stored in the binary file
  TIME (s)   : Timestamp in seconds from start of recording
  CH         : Channel ID (0 to 3); records are interleaved across channels
  RAW        : Raw 12-bit ADC integer reading (0 to 4095)
  VOLTAGE (V): Computed from raw_value - your program must do this conversion
  TEMP (C)   : Sensor temperature; stored as tenths of a degree in the binary
               (e.g. binary field value 245 = 24.5 C, shown here as 24.5)
  FLAGS      : status_flags byte in hex
               Bit 0 (0x01) = sensor fault
               Bit 1 (0x02) = out of range
               0x00 = no flags set  |  0x01 = fault  |  0x03 = fault + OOR
  SEQ        : Sequence number; should increment by 1 each record
               A jump of more than 1 indicates lost/missing data

==========================================================================================
  WHAT TO LOOK FOR
==========================================================================================

  Before writing any code, spend time reading this file. Ask yourself:

  - How are the four channels interleaved? What pattern do you see in the CH column?
  - What is the typical voltage range for each channel?
  - Can you spot any records where the voltage looks unusual?
  - Are there any records where FLAGS is not 0x00? What does that mean?
  - Does the SEQ column always increment by exactly 1?
    If not, where does it jump, and by how much?
  - How does the TEMP column vary? Are there any unusually high readings?

  These are exactly the questions your program must answer automatically.
  Understanding the data first will make the code much clearer to write.

==========================================================================================
